        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="2048" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/187_1003703_africa_dxm.png/220px-187_1003703_africa_dxm.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/187_1003703_africa_dxm.png/330px-187_1003703_africa_dxm.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/187_1003703_africa_dxm.png/440px-187_1003703_africa_dxm.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:187_1003703_africa_dxm.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Satellite photo of Africa. The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" title="Sahara Desert">
         Sahara Desert
        </a>
        in the north can be clearly seen.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="1200" height="73" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg/220px-Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg/330px-Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg/440px-Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Africa-asia-america-to-scale.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A composite satellite image of Africa (centre) with North America (left) and Eurasia (right), to scale
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Africa is the largest of the three great southward projections from the largest landmass of the Earth. Separated from Europe by the
      <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
       Mediterranean Sea
      </a>
      , it is joined to Asia at its northeast extremity by the
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
       Isthmus of Suez
      </a>
      (transected by the
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
       Suez Canal
      </a>
      ), 163 km (101 mi) wide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        [72]
       </a>
      </sup>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">
       Geopolitically
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">
       Sinai Peninsula
      </a>
      east of the Suez Canal is often considered part of Africa, as well.)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        [73]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From the most northerly point,
      <a href="/wiki/Ras_ben_Sakka" title="Ras ben Sakka">
       Ras ben Sakka
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">
       Tunisia
      </a>
      (37°21' N), to the most southerly point,
      <a href="/wiki/Cape_Agulhas" title="Cape Agulhas">
       Cape Agulhas
      </a>
      in South Africa (34°51'15" S), is a distance of approximately 8,000 km (5,000 mi);
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Cap-Vert" title="Cap-Vert">
       Cape Verde
      </a>
      , 17°33'22" W, the westernmost point, to
      <a href="/wiki/Ras_Hafun" title="Ras Hafun">
       Ras Hafun
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">
       Somalia
      </a>
      , 51°27'52" E, the most easterly projection, is a distance of approximately 7,400 km (4,600 mi).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MW_75-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MW-75">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The coastline is 26,000 km (16,000 mi) long, and the absence of deep indentations of the shore is illustrated by the fact that Europe, which covers only 10,400,000 km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      (4,000,000 sq mi) – about a third of the surface of Africa – has a coastline of 32,000 km (20,000 mi).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MW_75-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-MW-75">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Africa's largest country is
      <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
       Algeria
      </a>
      , and its smallest country is the
      <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">
       Seychelles
      </a>
      , an
      <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">
       archipelago
      </a>
      off the east coast.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoare_76-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hoare-76">
        [76]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The smallest nation on the continental mainland is
      <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">
       The Gambia
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Geologically, Africa includes the
      <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">
       Arabian Peninsula
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">
       Zagros Mountains
      </a>
      of Iran and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatolian_Plateau" title="Anatolian Plateau">
       Anatolian Plateau
      </a>
      of Turkey mark where the
      <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">
       African Plate
      </a>
      collided with Eurasia. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrotropic_ecozone" title="Afrotropic ecozone">
       Afrotropic ecozone
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Saharo-Arabian_Region" title="Saharo-Arabian Region">
       Saharo-Arabian desert
      </a>
      to its north unite the region biogeographically, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">
       Afro-Asiatic
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">
       language family
      </a>
      unites the north linguistically.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
       Climate
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Africa" title="Climate of Africa">
       Climate of Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Africa_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Africa map of Köppen climate classification
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The climate of Africa ranges from
      <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">
       tropical
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Subarctic" title="Subarctic">
       subarctic
      </a>
      on its highest peaks. Its northern half is primarily
      <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">
       desert
      </a>
      , or
      <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">
       arid
      </a>
      , while its central and southern areas contain both
      <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">
       savanna
      </a>
      plains and dense
      <a href="/wiki/Jungle" title="Jungle">
       jungle
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">
       rainforest
      </a>
      ) regions. In between, there is a convergence, where vegetation patterns such as
      <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">
       sahel
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">
       steppe
      </a>
      dominate. Africa is the hottest continent on earth and 60% of the entire land surface consists of drylands and deserts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-environmentalatlas_77-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-environmentalatlas-77">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The record for the highest-ever recorded temperature, in
      <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
       Libya
      </a>
      in 1922 (58 °C (136 °F)), was discredited in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newRecord_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-newRecord-78">
        [78]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">
       Fauna
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Africa" title="Fauna of Africa">
       Fauna of Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zebras,_Serengeti_savana_plains,_Tanzania.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="1024" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Zebras%2C_Serengeti_savana_plains%2C_Tanzania.jpg/220px-Zebras%2C_Serengeti_savana_plains%2C_Tanzania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Zebras%2C_Serengeti_savana_plains%2C_Tanzania.jpg/330px-Zebras%2C_Serengeti_savana_plains%2C_Tanzania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Zebras%2C_Serengeti_savana_plains%2C_Tanzania.jpg/440px-Zebras%2C_Serengeti_savana_plains%2C_Tanzania.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zebras,_Serengeti_savana_plains,_Tanzania.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Savanna at
        <a href="/wiki/Ngorongoro_Conservation_Area" title="Ngorongoro Conservation Area">
         Ngorongoro Conservation Area
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">
         Tanzania
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Africa boasts perhaps the world's largest combination of density and "range of freedom" of
      <a href="/wiki/Wild_animal" title="Wild animal">
       wild animal
      </a>
      populations and diversity, with wild populations of large
      <a href="/wiki/Carnivore" title="Carnivore">
       carnivores
      </a>
      (such as
      <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">
       lions
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hyena" title="Hyena">
       hyenas
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Cheetah" title="Cheetah">
       cheetahs
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Herbivore" title="Herbivore">
       herbivores
      </a>
      (such as
      <a href="/wiki/African_buffalo" title="African buffalo">
       buffalo
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">
       elephants
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Camel" title="Camel">
       camels
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Giraffe" title="Giraffe">
       giraffes
      </a>
      ) ranging freely on primarily open non-private plains. It is also home to a variety of "jungle" animals including
      <a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">
       snakes
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">
       primates
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Aquatic_ecosystem" title="Aquatic ecosystem">
       aquatic life
      </a>
      such as
      <a href="/wiki/Crocodile" title="Crocodile">
       crocodiles
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">
       amphibians
      </a>
      . In addition, Africa has the largest number of
      <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">
       megafauna
      </a>
      species, as it was least affected by the
      <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_extinction_event#The_Pleistocene_or_Ice_Age_extinction_event" title="Quaternary extinction event">
       extinction of the Pleistocene megafauna
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology_and_biodiversity">
       Ecology and biodiversity
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_beach.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/220px-Mauritius_beach.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/330px-Mauritius_beach.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/440px-Mauritius_beach.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_beach.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Tropical beach in
        <a href="/wiki/Trou-aux-Biches" title="Trou-aux-Biches">
         Trou-aux-Biches
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">
         Mauritius
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Africa has over 3,000
      <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">
       protected areas
      </a>
      , with 198 marine protected areas, 50 biosphere reserves, and 80 wetlands reserves. Significant habitat destruction, increases in human population and poaching are reducing Africa's biological diversity and
      <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">
       arable land
      </a>
      . Human encroachment, civil unrest and the introduction of non-native species threaten biodiversity in Africa. This has been exacerbated by administrative problems, inadequate personnel and funding problems.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-environmentalatlas_77-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-environmentalatlas-77">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
       Deforestation
      </a>
      is affecting Africa at twice the world rate, according to the United Nations Environment Programme (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNEP" title="UNEP">
       UNEP
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the University of Pennsylvania African Studies Center, 31% of Africa's pasture lands and 19% of its forests and woodlands are classified as degraded, and Africa is losing over four million hectares of forest per year, which is twice the average deforestation rate for the rest of the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-environmentalatlas_77-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-environmentalatlas-77">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some sources claim that approximately 90% of the original, virgin forests in
      <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">
       West Africa
      </a>
      have been destroyed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Over 90% of
      <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">
       Madagascar
      </a>
      's original forests have been destroyed since the arrival of humans 2000 years ago.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
      About 65% of Africa's agricultural land suffers from soil degradation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrotropic_ecozone" title="Afrotropic ecozone">
       Afrotropic ecozone
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palearctic_ecozone" title="Palearctic ecozone">
       Palearctic ecozone
      </a>
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
       Politics
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Africa_by_country" title="List of political parties in Africa by country">
       List of political parties in Africa by country
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      There are clear signs of increased networking among African organizations and states. For example, in the civil war in the
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">
       Democratic Republic of the Congo
      </a>
      (former
      <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">
       Zaire
      </a>
      ), rather than rich, non-African countries intervening, neighbouring African countries became involved (see also
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">
       Second Congo War
      </a>
      ). Since the conflict began in 1998, the estimated death toll has reached 5 million.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_African_Union">
       The African Union
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1000" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg/170px-Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg/255px-Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg/340px-Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg.png 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_African_Union_with_Suspended_States.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of the African Union with suspended states highlighted in light green
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
       African Union
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
       African Union
      </a>
      (AU) is a 54-member federation consisting of all of Africa's states except
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      . The union was formed, with
      <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">
       Addis Ababa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopia
      </a>
      , as its headquarters, on 26 June 2001. The union was officially established on 9 July 2002
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-African_Union_2002_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-African_Union_2002-84">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
      as a successor to the
      <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">
       Organisation of African Unity
      </a>
      (OAU). In July 2004, the African Union's
      <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">
       Pan-African Parliament
      </a>
      (PAP) was relocated to
      <a href="/wiki/Midrand" title="Midrand">
       Midrand
      </a>
      , in South Africa, but the
      <a href="/wiki/African_Commission_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights">
       African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights
      </a>
      remained in Addis Ababa. There is a policy in effect to decentralize the African Federation's institutions so that they are shared by all the states.
     </p>
     <p>
      The African Union, not to be confused with the AU Commission, is formed by the
      <a href="/wiki/Constitutive_Act_of_the_African_Union" title="Constitutive Act of the African Union">
       Constitutive Act of the African Union
      </a>
      , which aims to transform the
      <a href="/wiki/African_Economic_Community" title="African Economic Community">
       African Economic Community
      </a>
      , a federated commonwealth, into a state under established international conventions. The African Union has a parliamentary government, known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">
       African Union Government
      </a>
      , consisting of legislative, judicial and executive organs. It is led by the African Union President and Head of State, who is also the President of the
      <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">
       Pan-African Parliament
      </a>
      . A person becomes AU President by being elected to the PAP, and subsequently gaining majority support in the PAP. The powers and authority of the President of the African Parliament derive from the Constitutive Act and the
      <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">
       Protocol of the Pan-African Parliament
      </a>
      , as well as the inheritance of presidential authority stipulated by African treaties and by international treaties, including those subordinating the Secretary General of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OAU" title="OAU">
       OAU
      </a>
      Secretariat (AU Commission) to the PAP. The government of the AU consists of all-union (federal), regional, state, and municipal authorities, as well as hundreds of institutions, that together manage the day-to-day affairs of the institution.
     </p>
     <p>
      Political associations such as the African Union offer hope for greater co-operation and peace between the continent's many countries. Extensive human rights abuses still occur in several parts of Africa, often under the oversight of the state. Most of such violations occur for political reasons, often as a side effect of civil war. Countries where major human rights violations have been reported in recent times include the
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">
       Democratic Republic of the Congo
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">
       Sierra Leone
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">
       Liberia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">
       Sudan
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">
       Zimbabwe
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">
       Côte d'Ivoire
      </a>
      .
     </p>

         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/23px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/35px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/45px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
         Egypt
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        286,538
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>

       </td>
       <td align="left">
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Algeria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Algeria.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

        </a>
       </td>

       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        5
       </td>
       <td align="left">
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/23px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/35px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Flag_of_Angola.svg/45px-Flag_of_Angola.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

       </td>

        </span>

      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        8
       </td>
       <td align="left">
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Kenya.svg/23px-Flag_of_Kenya.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Kenya.svg/35px-Flag_of_Kenya.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Flag_of_Kenya.svg/45px-Flag_of_Kenya.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">
         Kenya
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        60,937
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        9
       </td>
       <td align="left">
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="720" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Flag_of_Ethiopia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Ethiopia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Flag_of_Ethiopia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Ethiopia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Flag_of_Ethiopia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Ethiopia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
