         Ethiopia
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        54,809
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        10
       </td>
       <td align="left">
        <span class="flagicon">
         <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">
         Tanzania
        </a>
       </td>
       <td>
        49,115
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Although it has abundant
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">
       natural resources
      </a>
      , Africa remains the world's poorest and most
      <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">
       underdeveloped
      </a>
      continent, the result of a variety of causes that may include
      <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">
       corrupt governments
      </a>
      that have often committed serious
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations" title="Human rights violations">
       human rights violations
      </a>
      , failed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_planning" title="Central planning">
       central planning
      </a>
      , high levels of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illiteracy" title="Illiteracy">
       illiteracy
      </a>
      , lack of access to foreign capital, and frequent tribal and military conflict (ranging from
      <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">
       guerrilla warfare
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        [85]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      ' Human Development Report in 2003, the bottom 24 ranked nations (151st to 175th) were all African.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        [86]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Africa" title="Poverty in Africa">
       Poverty
      </a>
      , illiteracy,
      <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">
       malnutrition
      </a>
      and inadequate water supply and sanitation, as well as poor health, affect a large proportion of the people who reside in the African continent. In August 2008, the World Bank
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        [87]
       </a>
      </sup>
      announced revised global poverty estimates based on a new international poverty line of $1.25 per day (versus the previous measure of $1.00). 80.5% of the
      <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
       Sub-Saharan Africa
      </a>
      population was living on less than $2.50 (PPP) per day in 2005, compared with 85.7% for
      <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
       India
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Sub-Saharan Africa is the least successful region of the world in reducing poverty ($1.25 per day); some 50% of
      <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Africa" title="Poverty in Africa">
       the population living in poverty
      </a>
      in 1981 (200 million people), a figure that rose to 58% in 1996 before dropping to 50% in 2005 (380 million people). The average poor person in sub-Saharan Africa is estimated to live on only 70 cents per day, and was poorer in 2003 than in 1973,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        [89]
       </a>
      </sup>
      indicating increasing poverty in some areas. Some of it is attributed to unsuccessful economic liberalization programmes spearheaded by foreign companies and governments, but other studies have cited bad domestic government policies more than external factors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        [90]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        [91]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From 1995 to 2005, Africa's rate of economic growth increased, averaging 5% in 2005. Some countries experienced still higher growth rates, notably
      <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">
       Angola
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">
       Sudan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">
       Equatorial Guinea
      </a>
      , all of which had recently begun extracting their
      <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
       petroleum
      </a>
      reserves or had expanded their
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_extraction" title="Oil extraction">
       oil extraction
      </a>
      capacity. The continent is believed to hold 90% of the world's
      <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">
       cobalt
      </a>
      , 90% of its
      <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">
       platinum
      </a>
      , 50% of its
      <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">
       gold
      </a>
      , 98% of its
      <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">
       chromium
      </a>
      , 70% of its
      <a href="/wiki/Tantalite" title="Tantalite">
       tantalite
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        [93]
       </a>
      </sup>
      64% of its
      <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">
       manganese
      </a>
      and one-third of its
      <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">
       uranium
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">
       Democratic Republic of the Congo
      </a>
      (DRC) has 70% of the world's
      <a href="/wiki/Coltan" title="Coltan">
       coltan
      </a>
      , a mineral used in the production of
      <a href="/wiki/Tantalum_capacitor" title="Tantalum capacitor">
       tantalum capacitors
      </a>
      for electronic devices such as cell phones. The DRC also has more than 30% of the world's
      <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">
       diamond
      </a>
      reserves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        [95]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">
       Guinea
      </a>
      is the world's largest exporter of
      <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">
       bauxite
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        [96]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As the growth in Africa has been driven mainly by services and not manufacturing or agriculture, it has been growth without jobs and without reduction in
      <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Africa" title="Poverty in Africa">
       poverty
      </a>
      levels. In fact, the food security crisis of 2008 which took place on the heels of the global financial crisis has pushed back 100 million people into food insecurity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In recent years, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">
       People's Republic of China
      </a>
      has built increasingly stronger ties with African nations and is Africa's largest trading partner. In 2007, Chinese companies invested a total of US$1 billion in Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Africa_70-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Africa-70">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A Harvard University study led by professor
      <a href="/wiki/Calestous_Juma" title="Calestous Juma">
       Calestous Juma
      </a>
      showed that Africa could feed itself by making the transition from importer to self-sufficiency. "African agriculture is at the crossroads; we have come to the end of a century of policies that favoured Africa's export of raw materials and importation of food. Africa is starting to focus on agricultural innovation as its new engine for regional trade and prosperity."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        [98]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During US President Barack Obama's visit to Africa in July 2013, he announced a
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
       US$
      </a>
      7 billion plan to further develop infrastructure and work more intensively with African heads of state. He also announced a new programme named Trade Africa, designed to boost trade within the continent as well as between Africa and the US.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        [99]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main articles:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_people" title="African people">
       African people
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Africa" title="Demographics of Africa">
       Demographics of Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kobli1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1626" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Kobli1.jpg/220px-Kobli1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Kobli1.jpg/330px-Kobli1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Kobli1.jpg/440px-Kobli1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kobli1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Woman from
        <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">
         Benin
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Africa's population has rapidly increased over the last 40 years, and consequently, it is relatively young. In some African states, more than half the population is under 25 years of age.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        [100]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The total number of people in Africa increased from 229 million in 1950 to 630 million in 1990.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        [101]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2014, the population of Africa is estimated at 1.2 billion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Africa's total population surpassing other continents is fairly recent; African population surpassed Europe in the 1990s, while the
      <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
       Americas
      </a>
      was overtaken sometime around the year 2000; Africa's rapid population growth is expected to overtake the only two nations currently larger than its population, at roughly the same time - India and China's 1.4 billion people each will swap ranking around the year 2022.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        [103]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_tribesman.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3222" data-file-width="2153" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/San_tribesman.jpg/170px-San_tribesman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/San_tribesman.jpg/255px-San_tribesman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/San_tribesman.jpg/340px-San_tribesman.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_tribesman.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bushmen" title="Bushmen">
         San
        </a>
        Bushman man from
        <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">
         Botswana
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Speakers of
      <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">
       Bantu languages
      </a>
      (part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Niger%E2%80%93Congo_languages" title="Niger–Congo languages">
       Niger–Congo
      </a>
      family) are the majority in southern, central and southeast Africa. The Bantu-speaking peoples from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sahel" title="The Sahel">
       The Sahel
      </a>
      progressively expanded over most of Sub-Saharan Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        [104]
       </a>
      </sup>
      But there are also several
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nilotic" title="Nilotic">
       Nilotic
      </a>
      groups in
      <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">
       South Sudan
      </a>
      and East Africa, the mixed
      <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">
       Swahili people
      </a>
      on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swahili_Coast" title="Swahili Coast">
       Swahili Coast
      </a>
      , and a few remaining
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Africa" title="Indigenous peoples of Africa">
       indigenous
      </a>
      Khoisan ("
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bushmen" title="Bushmen">
       San"
      </a>
      or "Bushmen") and
      <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">
       Pygmy peoples
      </a>
      in southern and central Africa, respectively. Bantu-speaking Africans also predominate in Gabon and Equatorial Guinea, and are found in parts of southern Cameroon. In the
      <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">
       Kalahari Desert
      </a>
      of Southern Africa, the distinct people known as the Bushmen (also "San", closely related to, but distinct from "
      <a href="/wiki/Khoikhoi" title="Khoikhoi">
       Hottentots
      </a>
      ") have long been present. The San are physically distinct from other Africans and are the indigenous people of southern Africa. Pygmies are the pre-Bantu indigenous peoples of central Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        [105]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The peoples of West Africa primarily speak
      <a href="/wiki/Niger%E2%80%93Congo_languages" title="Niger–Congo languages">
       Niger–Congo languages
      </a>
      , belonging mostly to its non-Bantu branches, though some
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan" title="Nilo-Saharan">
       Nilo-Saharan
      </a>
      and Afro-Asiatic speaking groups are also found. The Niger–Congo-speaking
      <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">
       Yoruba
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Igbo_language" title="Igbo language">
       Igbo
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fulani" title="Fulani">
       Fulani
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Akan_language" title="Akan language">
       Akan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Wolof_people" title="Wolof people">
       Wolof
      </a>
      ethnic groups are the largest and most influential. In the central Sahara,
      <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">
       Mandinka
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Mande_languages" title="Mande languages">
       Mande
      </a>
      groups are most significant. Chadic-speaking groups, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Hausa_language" title="Hausa language">
       Hausa
      </a>
      , are found in more northerly parts of the region nearest to the Sahara, and Nilo-Saharan communities, such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Songhai_people" title="Songhai people">
       Songhai
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kanuri_people" title="Kanuri people">
       Kanuri
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zarma_people" title="Zarma people">
       Zarma
      </a>
      , are found in the eastern parts of West Africa bordering
      <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">
       Central Africa
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The peoples of North Africa consist of three main indigenous groups: Berbers in the northwest, Egyptians in the northeast, and Nilo-Saharan-speaking peoples in the east. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
       Arabs
      </a>
      who arrived in the 7th century AD introduced the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
       Arabic language
      </a>
      and Islam to North Africa. The Semitic
      <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
       Phoenicians
      </a>
      (who founded
      <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">
       Carthage
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Hyksos" title="Hyksos">
       Hyksos
      </a>
      , the Indo-Iranian
      <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">
       Alans
      </a>
      , the Indo- European
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
       Greeks
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
       Romans
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">
       Vandals
      </a>
      settled in North Africa as well. Significant Berber communities remain within
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
       Algeria
      </a>
      in the 21st century, while, to a lesser extent, Berber speakers are also present in some regions of Tunisia and Libya.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        [106]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Berber-speaking
      <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">
       Tuareg
      </a>
      and other often-
      <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">
       nomadic
      </a>
      peoples are the principal inhabitants of the Saharan interior of North Africa. In Mauritania, there is a small but near-extinct Berber community in the north and Niger–Congo-speaking peoples in the south, though in both regions Arabic and Arab culture predominates. In Sudan, although Arabic and Arab culture predominate, it is mostly inhabited by groups that originally spoke Nilo-Saharan, such as the Nubians, Fur, Masalit and Zaghawa, who, over the centuries, have variously intermixed with migrants from the Arabian peninsula. Small communities of Afro-Asiatic-speaking Beja nomads can also be found in Egypt and Sudan.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bedscha.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="600" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bedscha.jpg/220px-Bedscha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bedscha.jpg/330px-Bedscha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bedscha.jpg/440px-Bedscha.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bedscha.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Beja_people" title="Beja people">
         Beja
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">
         bedouins
        </a>
        from Northeast Africa
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">
       Horn of Africa
      </a>
      , some Ethiopian and
      <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">
       Eritrean
      </a>
      groups (like the
      <a href="/wiki/Amhara_people" title="Amhara people">
       Amhara
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tigray-Tigrinya_people" title="Tigray-Tigrinya people">
       Tigrayans
      </a>
      , collectively known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habesha_people" title="Habesha people">
       Habesha
      </a>
      ) speak languages from the
      <a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">
       Semitic
      </a>
      branch of the
      <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">
       Afro-Asiatic
      </a>
      language family, while the
      <a href="/wiki/Oromo_people" title="Oromo people">
       Oromo
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Somali_people" title="Somali people">
       Somali
      </a>
      speak languages from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cushitic" title="Cushitic">
       Cushitic
      </a>
      branch of Afro-Asiatic.
     </p>
     <p>
      Prior to the
      <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">
       decolonization
      </a>
      movements of the post-
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
       World War II
      </a>
      era,
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">
       Europeans
      </a>
      were represented in every part of Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Decolonization during the 1960s and 1970s often resulted in the mass emigration of white settlers – especially from Algeria and Morocco (1.6 million
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pieds-noir" title="Pieds-noir">
        pieds-noirs
       </a>
      </i>
      in North Africa),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kenya, Congo,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        [109]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Rhodesia, Mozambique and Angola.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Between 1975 and 1977, over a million colonials returned to Portugal alone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless,
      <a href="/wiki/White_Africans_of_European_ancestry" title="White Africans of European ancestry">
       white Africans
      </a>
      remain an important minority in many African states, particularly
      <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">
       Zimbabwe
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">
       Namibia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">
       Réunion
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_South_Africa" title="Republic of South Africa">
       Republic of South Africa
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        [112]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The country with the largest white African population is South Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        [113]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">
       Dutch
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/British_diaspora_in_Africa" title="British diaspora in Africa">
       British
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">
       diasporas
      </a>
      represent the largest communities of European ancestry on the continent today.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_114-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World-114">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      European colonization also brought sizable groups of
      <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">
       Asians
      </a>
      , particularly from the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">
       Indian subcontinent
      </a>
      , to British colonies. Large
      <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">
       Indian communities
      </a>
      are found in South Africa, and smaller ones are present in Kenya, Tanzania, and some other southern and southeast African countries. The large
      <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Uganda" title="Indians in Uganda">
       Indian community in Uganda
      </a>
      was
      <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Asians_from_Uganda" title="Expulsion of Asians from Uganda">
       expelled
      </a>
      by the dictator
      <a href="/wiki/Idi_Amin" title="Idi Amin">
       Idi Amin
      </a>
      in 1972, though many have since returned. The islands in the Indian Ocean are also populated primarily by people of Asian origin, often mixed with Africans and Europeans. The
      <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">
       Malagasy people
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">
       Madagascar
      </a>
      are an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" title="Austronesian people">
       Austronesian people
      </a>
      , but those along the coast are generally mixed with Bantu, Arab, Indian and European origins. Malay and Indian ancestries are also important components in the group of people known in South Africa as
      <a href="/wiki/Cape_Coloureds" title="Cape Coloureds">
       Cape Coloureds
      </a>
      (people with origins in two or more races and continents). During the 20th century, small but economically important communities of
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Lebanon#The_Lebanese_Diaspora" title="Demographics of Lebanon">
       Lebanese
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">
       Chinese
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Africa_70-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Africa-70">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
      have also developed in the larger coastal cities of
      <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">
       West
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">
       East Africa
      </a>
      , respectively.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
       Languages
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">
       Languages of Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2984" data-file-width="2502" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg/170px-Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg/255px-Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg/340px-Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Africa_ethnic_groups_1996.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map showing the traditional language families represented in Africa:
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E6EAAD; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">
          Afroasiatic
         </a>
         (Semitic-Hamitic)
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8E7D8F; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">
          Austronesian
         </a>
         (Malay-Polynesian)
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8A421A; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
          Indo-European
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #DC782D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">
          Khoisan
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niger-Congo_languages" title="Niger-Congo languages">
         Niger-Congo
        </a>
        :
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A6BE50; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">
          Bantu
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E9A96C; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Central and Eastern Sudanese
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #51384E; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Central Bantoid
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C96273; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Eastern Bantoid
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A7BC47; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Guinean
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #B77B85; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Mande_languages" title="Mande languages">
          Mande
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #4D7830; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         Western Bantoid
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">
         Nilo-Saharan
        </a>
        :
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #827241; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Kanuri_language" title="Kanuri language">
          Kanuri
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #824240; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_languages" title="Nilotic languages">
          Nilotic
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="legend">
         <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C88C50; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Songhay_languages" title="Songhay languages">
          Songhai
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      By most estimates, well over a thousand
      <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
       languages
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
       UNESCO
      </a>
      has estimated around two thousand) are spoken in Africa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most are of African origin, though some are of European or Asian origin. Africa is the most
      <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">
       multilingual
      </a>
      continent in the world, and it is not rare for individuals to fluently speak not only multiple African languages, but one or more European ones as well. There are four major
      <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">
       language families
      </a>
      indigenous to Africa:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages" title="Afroasiatic languages">
        <i>
         Afroasiatic
        </i>
       </a>
       languages are a language family of about 240 languages and 285 million people widespread throughout the
       <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">
        Horn of Africa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North Africa
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">
        Sahel
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southwest_Asia" title="Southwest Asia">
        Southwest Asia
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Nilo-Saharan_languages" title="Nilo-Saharan languages">
        <i>
         Nilo-Saharan
        </i>
       </a>
       language family consists of more than a hundred languages spoken by 30 million people. Nilo-Saharan languages are spoken by ethnic groups in
       <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">
        Chad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
        Ethiopia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">
        Kenya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
        Nigeria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">
        Sudan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">
        South Sudan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">
        Uganda
       </a>
       , and northern
       <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">
        Tanzania
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Niger%E2%80%93Congo_languages" title="Niger–Congo languages">
        <i>
         Niger–Congo
        </i>
       </a>
       language family covers much of Sub-Saharan Africa and is probably the largest language family in the world in terms of different languages.
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">
        <i>
         Khoisan
        </i>
       </a>
       languages number about fifty and are spoken in
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">
        Southern Africa
       </a>
       by approximately 120,000 people. Many of the Khoisan languages are
       <a href="/wiki/Endangered_language" title="Endangered language">
        endangered
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Khoikhoi" title="Khoikhoi">
        Khoi
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bushmen" title="Bushmen">
        San
       </a>
       peoples are considered the original inhabitants of this part of Africa.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Following the end of
      <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">
       colonialism
      </a>
      , nearly all African countries adopted
      <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
       official languages
      </a>
      that originated outside the continent, although several countries also granted legal recognition to indigenous languages (such as
      <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">
       Swahili
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">
       Yoruba
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Igbo_language" title="Igbo language">
       Igbo
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hausa_language" title="Hausa language">
       Hausa
      </a>
      ). In numerous countries,
      <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
       English
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
       French
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       see
       <a href="/wiki/African_French" title="African French">
        African French
       </a>
      </i>
      ) are used for communication in the public sphere such as government, commerce, education and the media.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
       Arabic
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">
       Afrikaans
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
       Spanish
      </a>
      are examples of languages that trace their origin to outside of Africa, and that are used by millions of Africans today, both in the public and private spheres.
      <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
       Italian
      </a>
      is spoken by some in former
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Colonial_Empire" title="Italian Colonial Empire">
       Italian colonies
      </a>
      in Africa.
      <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
       German
      </a>
      is spoken in
      <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">
       Namibia
      </a>
      , as it was a former
      <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
       German
      </a>
      protectorate.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
       Culture
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="2848" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg/220px-Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg/330px-Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg/440px-Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bet_Giyorgis_church_Lalibela_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The rock-hewn
        <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_George,_Lalibela" title="Church of Saint George, Lalibela">
         Church of Saint George
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Lalibela" title="Lalibela">
         Lalibela
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
         Ethiopia
        </a>
        is a
        <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
         UNESCO World Heritage Site
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Africa" title="Culture of Africa">
       Culture of Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Some aspects of traditional African cultures have become less practised in recent years as a result of neglect and suppression by colonial and post-colonial regimes. For example, African customs were discouraged, and African languages were prohibited in mission schools.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pearsonhighered.com_117-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pearsonhighered.com-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Leopold II of Belgium attempted to "civilize" Africans by discouraging polygamy and witchcraft.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pearsonhighered.com_117-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pearsonhighered.com-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Obidoh Freeborn posits that colonialism is one element that has created the character of modern African art.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to authors Douglas Fraser and Herbert M. Cole, "The precipitous alterations in the power structure wrought by colonialism were quickly followed by drastic iconographic changes in the art."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-119">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Fraser and Cole assert that, in Igboland, some art objects "lack the vigor and careful craftsmanship of the earlier art objects that served traditional functions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_119-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-119">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Author Chika Okeke-Agulu states that "the racist infrastructure of British imperial enterprise forced upon the political and cultural guardians of empire a denial and suppression of an emergent sovereign Africa and modernist art."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Soweto, the West Rand Administrative Board established a Cultural Section to collect, read, and review scripts before performances could occur.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Editors F. Abiola Irele and Simon Gikandi comment that the current identity of African literature had its genesis in the "traumatic encounter between Africa and Europe."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On the other hand, Mhoze Chikowero believes that Africans deployed music, dance, spirituality, and other performative cultures to (re)asset themselves as active agents and indigenous intellectuals, to unmake their colonial marginalization and reshape their own destinies."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There is now a resurgence in the attempts to rediscover and revalue African traditional cultures, under such movements as the
      <a href="/wiki/African_Renaissance" title="African Renaissance">
       African Renaissance
      </a>
      , led by
      <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">
       Thabo Mbeki
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Afrocentrism" title="Afrocentrism">
       Afrocentrism
      </a>
      , led by a group of scholars, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molefi_Asante" title="Molefi Asante">
       Molefi Asante
      </a>
      , as well as the increasing recognition of traditional spiritualism through decriminalization of
      <a href="/wiki/West_African_Vodun" title="West African Vodun">
       Vodou
      </a>
      and other forms of spirituality.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_art_and_architecture">
       Visual art and architecture
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/African_art" title="African art">
       African art
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Africa" title="Architecture of Africa">
       architecture
      </a>
      reflect the diversity of African cultures. The region's oldest known
      <a href="/wiki/Bead" title="Bead">
       beads
      </a>
      were made from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nassarius" title="Nassarius">
        Nassarius
       </a>
      </i>
      shells and worn as personal ornaments 72,000 years ago.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Pyramid_of_Giza" title="Great Pyramid of Giza">
       Great Pyramid of Giza
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </a>
      was the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_tallest_structure" title="World's tallest structure">
       world's tallest structure
      </a>
      for 4,000 years, until the completion of
      <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Cathedral" title="Lincoln Cathedral">
       Lincoln Cathedral
      </a>
      around the year 1300. The stone ruins of
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Zimbabwe" title="Great Zimbabwe">
       Great Zimbabwe
      </a>
      are also noteworthy for their architecture, as are the
      <a href="/wiki/Monolithic_church" title="Monolithic church">
       monolithic churches
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Lalibela" title="Lalibela">
       Lalibela
      </a>
      , Ethiopia, such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_George,_Lalibela" title="Church of Saint George, Lalibela">
       Church of Saint George
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1558" data-file-width="780" height="340" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg/170px-Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg/255px-Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg/340px-Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ke-Nako_Music-Performance_Vienna2008c.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A musician from
        <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">
         South Africa
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">
       Music and dance
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Africa" title="Music of Africa">
       Music of Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="900" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg/170px-Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg/255px-Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg/340px-Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Namibia_Rugby_Team.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Namibia national rugby union team">
         Namibia rugby team
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Egypt has long been a cultural focus of
      <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">
       the Arab world
      </a>
      , while remembrance of the rhythms of sub-Saharan Africa, in particular West Africa, was transmitted through the
      <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
       Atlantic slave trade
      </a>
      to modern
      <a href="/wiki/Samba" title="Samba">
       samba
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">
       blues
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
       jazz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">
       reggae
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">
       hip hop
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">
       rock
      </a>
      . The 1950s through the 1970s saw a conglomeration of these various styles with the popularization of
      <a href="/wiki/Afrobeat" title="Afrobeat">
       Afrobeat
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Highlife" title="Highlife">
       Highlife
      </a>
      music. Modern music of the continent includes the highly complex choral singing of southern Africa and the dance rhythms of the musical genre of
      <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">
       soukous
      </a>
      , dominated by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Music of the Democratic Republic of Congo">
       music of the Democratic Republic of Congo
      </a>
      . Indigenous musical and dance traditions of Africa are maintained by oral traditions, and they are distinct from the music and dance styles of
      <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
       North Africa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">
       Southern Africa
      </a>
      .
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">
       Arab
      </a>
      influences are visible in North African music and dance and, in Southern Africa,
      <a href="/wiki/Western_culture#Widespread_influence" title="Western culture">
       Western influences
      </a>
      are apparent due to
      <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">
       colonization
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
       Sports
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Fifty-four African countries have
      <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
       football (soccer)
      </a>
      teams in the
      <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">
       Confederation of African Football
      </a>
      . Egypt has won the African Cup seven times, and a record-making three times in a row. Cameroon, Nigeria, Senegal, Ghana, and Algeria have advanced to the knockout stage of recent
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
       FIFA World Cups
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">
       South Africa
      </a>
      hosted the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">
       2010 World Cup tournament
      </a>
      , becoming the first African country to do so.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">
       Cricket
      </a>
      is popular in some African nations.
      <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_cricket_team" title="South Africa national cricket team">
       South Africa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_national_cricket_team" title="Zimbabwe national cricket team">
       Zimbabwe
      </a>
      have
      <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">
       Test
      </a>
      status, while
      <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_cricket_team" title="Kenya national cricket team">
       Kenya
      </a>
      is the leading non-test team and previously had
      <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">
       One-Day International cricket
      </a>
      (ODI) status (from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President%27s_Cup_1997-98" title="President's Cup 1997-98">
       10 October 1997
      </a>
      , until
      <a href="/wiki/2014_Cricket_World_Cup_Qualifier#Super_Six" title="2014 Cricket World Cup Qualifier">
       30 January 2014
      </a>
      ). The three countries jointly hosted the
      <a href="/wiki/2003_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2003 Cricket World Cup">
       2003 Cricket World Cup
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_cricket_team" title="Namibia national cricket team">
       Namibia
      </a>
      is the other African country to have played in a World Cup.
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      in northern Africa has also hosted the
      <a href="/wiki/2002_Morocco_Cup" title="2002 Morocco Cup">
       2002 Morocco Cup
      </a>
      , but the national team has never qualified for a major tournament.
      <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">
       Rugby
      </a>
      is a popular sport in South Africa, Namibia, and Zimbabwe.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
       Religion
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Africa" title="Religion in Africa">
       Religion in Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Africans profess a wide variety of religious beliefs, and statistics on religious affiliation are difficult to come by since they are often a sensitive a topic for governments with mixed religious populations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stanford_125-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-stanford-125">
        [125]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_126-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT-126">
        [126]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the
      <a href="/wiki/World_Book_Encyclopedia" title="World Book Encyclopedia">
       World Book Encyclopedia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Africa" title="Islam in Africa">
       Islam
      </a>
      is the largest religion in Africa, followed by
      <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Africa" title="Christianity in Africa">
       Christianity
      </a>
      . According to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_Britannica" title="Encyclopedia Britannica">
       Encyclopedia Britannica
      </a>
      , 45% of the population are
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christians
      </a>
      , 40% are
      <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
       Muslims
      </a>
      , and 10% follow
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_Traditional_Religion" title="African Traditional Religion">
       traditional religions
      </a>
      . A small number of Africans are
      <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
       Hindu
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">
       Buddhist
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confucianist" title="Confucianist">
       Confucianist
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">
       Baha'i
      </a>
      , or have beliefs from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judaism_in_Africa" title="Judaism in Africa">
       Judaic tradition
      </a>
      . There is also a minority of Africans who are
      <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Africa" title="Irreligion in Africa">
       irreligious
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Territories_and_regions">
       Territories and regions
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Africa" title="List of regions of Africa">
       List of regions of Africa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Africa" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in Africa">
       List of sovereign states and dependent territories in Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The countries in this table are categorized according to the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme_for_Africa" title="United Nations geoscheme for Africa">
       scheme for geographic subregions
      </a>
      used by the United Nations, and data included are per sources in cross-referenced articles. Where they differ, provisos are clearly indicated.
     </p>
     <table style="width:155px; float:right; margin-right:0.0em;">
      <tr>
       <td>

         </cite>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAfrica&amp;rft.atitle=World+Meteorological+Organization+Assessment+of+the+Purported+World+Record+58%B0C+Temperature+Extreme+at+El+Azizia%2C+Libya+%2813+September+1922%29&amp;rft.aufirst=KI&amp;rft.aulast=El+Fadli&amp;rft.date=2012-09&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fjournals.ametsoc.org%2Fdoi%2Fpdf%2F10.1175%2FBAMS-D-12-00093.1&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1175%2FBAMS-D-12-00093.1&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.jtitle=Bulletin+of+the+American+Meteorological+Society&amp;rft.pages=199&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=94">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         (The 136 °F (57.8 °C), claimed by
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%27Aziziya" title="'Aziziya">
          'Aziziya
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">
          Libya
         </a>
         , on 13 September 1922, has been officially deemed invalid by the
         <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">
          World Meteorological Organization
         </a>
         .)
        </span>
       </li>

         <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
          Canary Islands
         </a>
         , of which
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">
          Las Palmas de Gran Canaria
         </a>
         are
         <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">
          Santa Cruz de Tenerife
         </a>
         are co-capitals, are often considered part of Northern Africa due to their relative proximity to
         <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
          Morocco
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">
          Western Sahara
         </a>
         ; population and area figures are for 2001.
         <br/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-131">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-131">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The Spanish
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">
          exclave
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">
          Ceuta
         </a>
         is surrounded on land by Morocco in Northern Africa; population and area figures are for 2001.
         <br/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-132">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-132">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
          Egypt
         </a>
         is generally considered a
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">
          transcontinental country
         </a>
         in Northern Africa (UN region) and Western Asia; population and area figures are for African portion only, west of the
         <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">
          Suez Canal
         </a>
         .
         <br/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-133">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-133">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The Portuguese
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madeira_Islands" title="Madeira Islands">
          Madeira Islands
         </a>
         are often considered part of Northern Africa due to their relative proximity to Morocco; population and area figures are for 2001.
         <br/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-134">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-134">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The Spanish
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">
          exclave
         </a>
         of
         <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">
          Melilla
         </a>
         is surrounded on land by Morocco in Northern Africa; population and area figures are for 2001.
         <br/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic-135">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic_135-0">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         The territory of
         <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">
          Western Sahara
         </a>
         is claimed by the
         <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">
          Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
          Morocco
         </a>
         . The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SADR" title="SADR">
          SADR
         </a>
         is recognized as a sovereign state by the
         <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
          African Union
         </a>
         .
         <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
          Morocco
         </a>
         claims the entirety of the country as its
         <a href="/wiki/Southern_Provinces" title="Southern Provinces">
          Southern Provinces
         </a>
         . Morocco administers 4/5 of the territory while the SADR controls 1/5. Morocco's annexation of this territory has not been recognized internationally.
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-136">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-136">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <a href="/wiki/Bloemfontein" title="Bloemfontein">
          Bloemfontein
         </a>
         is the judicial capital of South Africa, while
         <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">
          Cape Town
         </a>
         is its legislative seat, and
         <a href="/wiki/Pretoria" title="Pretoria">
          Pretoria
         </a>
         is the country's administrative seat.
         <br/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-137">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-137">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <a href="/wiki/Yamoussoukro" title="Yamoussoukro">
          Yamoussoukro
         </a>
         is the official capital of
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">
          Côte d'Ivoire
         </a>
         , while
         <a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">
          Abidjan
         </a>
         is the
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">
           de facto
          </a>
         </i>
         seat.
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>
